					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Fictional character from the Metal Gear series</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the video game character. For the MSX2 video game, see <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake" title="Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake">Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</a>. For the character's similarly-named brother, see <a href="/wiki/Solidus_Snake" class="mw-redirect" title="Solidus Snake">Solidus Snake</a>. For other characters in the franchise known as "Snake", see <a href="/wiki/Snake_(Metal_Gear)" title="Snake (Metal Gear)">Snake (Metal Gear)</a>.</div>

class="infobox-data">American</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Solid Snake</b><span style="font-weight: normal"> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>: <span lang="ja">ソリッド・スネーク</span>, <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn</a>: <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Soriddo Sunēku</i></span>)</span>, real name <b>David</b>, is a fictional character and one of the <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonists</a> of <a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear" title="Metal Gear">Metal Gear</a></i> series, created by <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a>. He is depicted as a former <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Special_Forces" title="United States Army Special Forces">Green Beret</a> and highly skilled <a href="/wiki/Special_operations" title="Special operations">special operations</a> soldier engaged in solo stealth and <a href="/wiki/Espionage" title="Espionage">espionage</a> missions who is often tasked with destroying models of the bipedal nuclear weapon-armed <a href="/wiki/Mecha" title="Mecha">mecha</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear</a>. Controlled by the player, he must act alone, supported via radio by commanding officers and specialists. While his first appearances in the original <i>Metal Gear</i> games were references to Hollywood films, the <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> series has given a consistent design by artist <a href="/wiki/Yoji_Shinkawa" title="Yoji Shinkawa">Yoji Shinkawa</a> alongside an established personality while also exploring his relationship with his <a href="/wiki/Big_Boss_(Metal_Gear)" title="Big Boss (Metal Gear)">mentor and father</a>.
</p><p>During the <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> games, the character has been voiced by voice actor <a href="/wiki/Akio_%C5%8Ctsuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Akio Ōtsuka">Akio Ōtsuka</a> in the Japanese version and by Canadian-American screenwriter and actor <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a> in the English version. He also appears in <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros." title="Super Smash Bros.">Super Smash Bros.</a></i> series as a playable fighter, as well as the battle royale game <i><a href="/wiki/Fortnite" title="Fortnite">Fortnite</a></i>. Considered to be one of the most iconic protagonists in video game history, Solid Snake has been acclaimed by critics, with his personality and both Ōtsuka's and Hayter's voice acting being noted as primary factors of the character's appeal.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Characteristics">Characteristics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Characteristics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the early games, Solid Snake's visual appearances were references to popular actors. He was given his own consistent design in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_(1998_video_game)" title="Metal Gear Solid (1998 video game)">Metal Gear Solid</a></i>. He also establishes Philanthropy, an anti-Metal Gear organization carrying the motto "To let the world be", with his friend <a href="/wiki/Otacon" class="mw-redirect" title="Otacon">Otacon</a>. In <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_4:_Guns_of_the_Patriots" title="Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots">Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</a></i>, he has access to OctoCamo, which allows him to change his appearance to match the surface he is leaning on. And FaceCamo, which can change his facial appearance to make him look like other characters, as well as his younger self.
</p><p>Snake possesses an <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQ</a> of 180 and is fluent in six languages. Solid Snake has been on the battlefield for most of his life,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and says that it is the only place he feels truly alive.<sup id="cite_ref-feelalive_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feelalive-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He is a hardened veteran, burying his emotions within himself during missions, every one of which has different motives.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He is also immediately shown as a loner,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> often with no intentions of taking orders from anyone anymore<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and he shows no sign of longing for the army or the country of which he was a part.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, along with these traits he has a more human side, being flirtatious,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> self-sacrificing<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and with a strong belief that even on a battlefield friendship<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and love<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> can flourish, and that violence is not glorious.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake's perceived stance on violence may be a case of denial, as Snake's enemies and at least one of his allies have claimed that he enjoys killing, and label him as more evil than the people he has killed.<sup id="cite_ref-feelalive_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feelalive-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  When he is not on duty, his favorite recreational activity is being a <a href="/wiki/Mushing" title="Mushing">musher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Appearances">Appearances</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Appearances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Video_games">Video games</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Video games"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Metal_Gear_and_Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake"><i>Metal Gear</i> and <i>Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Metal Gear and Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(video_game)" title="Metal Gear (video game)">Metal Gear</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake" title="Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake">Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</a></div>
<p><i>Metal Gear</i> introduces Snake, a rookie recruit of the elite special forces unit <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#FOXHOUND" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">FOXHOUND</a>. Snake is sent by Big Boss into <a href="/wiki/Outer_Heaven" class="mw-redirect" title="Outer Heaven">Outer Heaven</a>, a rogue nation in South Africa, to rescue <a href="/wiki/Gray_Fox_(Metal_Gear)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray Fox (Metal Gear)">Gray Fox</a> and discover who or what the "<a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear</a>" is.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As his mission progresses, Snake finds out that he has been set up; Big Boss's phantom intended to use TX-55 Metal Gear (the experimental, nuclear-armed weapon) to establish Outer Heaven as a nuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After destroying the Metal Gear, Snake confronts and defeats Big Boss's phantom.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The sequel <i>Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</i> sees Solid Snake called up to infiltrate Zanzibar Land, a heavily fortified enemy base in Central Asia that has aggravated an international oil crisis and declared themselves a nuclear power by kidnapping Dr. Kio Marv (after the creation of a bio-engineered algae that produces an oil substitute) and the Metal Gear engineer <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Dr._Madnar" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Pettrovich Madnar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake infiltrates the base and discovers that Pettrovich as well as Fox has defected to Zanzibar Land, and that Zanzibar Land is led by the true Big Boss.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake destroys Metal Gear D, and defeats both Fox and the true Big Boss.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UGO_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UGO-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Metal_Gear_Solid_/_The_Twin_Snakes"><span id="Metal_Gear_Solid_.2F_The_Twin_Snakes"></span><i>Metal Gear Solid / The Twin Snakes</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Metal Gear Solid / The Twin Snakes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_(1998_video_game)" title="Metal Gear Solid (1998 video game)">Metal Gear Solid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_The_Twin_Snakes" title="Metal Gear Solid: The Twin Snakes">Metal Gear Solid: The Twin Snakes</a></div>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid</i> and its remake – <i>The Twin Snakes</i> – reveals Solid Snake's real name as David<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">デビッド</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Debiddo</i></span>)</span>. He is pulled out of retirement by <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Roy_Campbell" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Roy Campbell</a> to deal with the "Sons of Big Boss" led by <a href="/wiki/Liquid_Snake" title="Liquid Snake">Liquid Snake</a> who seized an isolated American nuclear weapons disposal facility on Shadow Moses Island. Snake's mission is to rescue <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Donald_Anderson" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Donald Anderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Kenneth_Baker" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Kenneth Baker</a> but he is unable to prevent both hostages' deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As the game progresses, Snake infiltrates and learns about <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear_REX" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear REX</a> while meeting up with rookie soldier <a href="/wiki/Meryl_Silverburgh" class="mw-redirect" title="Meryl Silverburgh">Meryl Silverburgh</a> and REX's engineer <a href="/wiki/Otacon" class="mw-redirect" title="Otacon">Hal Emmerich</a>, confronts and defeats each member of the corrupt faction of FOXHOUND (consisting of <a href="/wiki/Revolver_Ocelot" title="Revolver Ocelot">Revolver Ocelot</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Decoy_Octopus" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Decoy Octopus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psycho_Mantis" title="Psycho Mantis">Psycho Mantis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sniper_Wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Sniper Wolf">Sniper Wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Vulcan_Raven" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Vulcan Raven</a>, and the Genome Soldiers), several confrontations with the Cyborg Ninja, is able to destroy REX, and personally confronts Liquid. During their fight, it is revealed that Solid and Liquid are twin brothers artificially conceived from Big Boss's genes during the "Les Enfants Terribles" government project designed to create the perfect soldier, in which one brother was genetically modified to be superior over the other.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Liquid harbors a strong resentment towards Snake since Solid was apparently given their father's dominant "soldier genes" and Liquid was seemingly cast aside. A grueling series of battles and Liquid dies from the FOXDIE virus that was previously implanted into Snake by <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Naomi_Hunter" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Naomi Hunter</a> in order to wipe out FOXHOUND without risking any damage to REX for retrieval.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the end, it is revealed that Liquid got Big Boss's superior "soldier genes" while Solid was actually the inferior one.<sup id="cite_ref-MGSpostcred_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MGSpostcred-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty"><i>Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty" title="Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty">Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</a></div>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty</i> shows Solid Snake as a central character. During the game's extensive prologue sequence, he is sent by Otacon's anti-<a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">proliferation</a> organization <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Philanthropy" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Philanthropy</a> to infiltrate a cargo tanker and photograph <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear_RAY" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear RAY</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the operation, however, RAY is hijacked and the tanker destroyed, with Snake apparently dead and framed for the deed.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the game's main portion, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Solidus_Snake" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Solidus Snake</a> steals Snake's identity,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and leads the "Sons of Liberty" (consisting of Revolver Ocelot, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Fortune" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Fortune</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Fatman" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Fatman</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Vamp" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Vamp</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Olga_Gurlukovich" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Olga Gurlukovich</a>) while Snake himself uses the pseudonym Iroquois Pliskin<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">イロコィ・プリスキン</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Irokoi Purisukin</i></span>)</span> as a non-playable character who assists rookie agent <a href="/wiki/Raiden_(Metal_Gear)" title="Raiden (Metal Gear)">Raiden</a> through the remote offshore Big Shell facility and in taking down Solidus and RAY while also learning about <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#The_Patriots" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">the Patriots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Metal_Gear_Solid_4:_Guns_of_the_Patriots"><i>Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</i></h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Snake_TGS_2010.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Old_Snake_TGS_2010.jpg/250px-Old_Snake_TGS_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Old_Snake_TGS_2010.jpg/500px-Old_Snake_TGS_2010.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a><figcaption>Old Snake cosplayer at Tokyo Game Show 2010</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_4:_Guns_of_the_Patriots" title="Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots">Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</a></div>
<p><i>Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the Patriots</i> features an aged incarnation of the character who nicknamed himself Old Snake<span style="font-weight: normal"> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">オールド・スネーク</span></span>, <span title="Hepburn transliteration"><i lang="ja-Latn">Ōrudo Sunēku</i></span>)</span> as the protagonist once again. Thanks to Otacon and <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Sunny" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Sunny</a>, he wears a sneaking suit outfitted with "Octocamo" technology which allows him to blend with his environment as well as a face mask which alters his appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For his final mission, he is once again enlisted by Campbell to assassinate Liquid Ocelot, CEO of a giant mother company that are trying to take control of the Patriots' AIs.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He also learns from Naomi that his life has been artificially shortened as part of the cloning process so that his genes can't be used as a weapon in later research, thus explaining why he has the physical appearance of an elderly man despite being only forty-two years old.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake and his allies are forced to destroy the Patriots' AI and fight through Ocelot's forces until Snake defeats Liquid's doppelgänger in hand-to-hand combat. Snake tried to commit suicide as his DNA contains a mutated FOXDIE virus that might trigger an epidemic, but Big Boss revealed a new variant overwrote the mutant version to which the two make up as father and son. David is told he still has a chance to live "not as a snake but as a man" so he decides to live out the remainder of his life in peace, vowing that he will live long enough to see what the future holds for the new world he has helped create.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other_appearances">Other appearances</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other appearances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> prequels alludes to Solid Snake's existence; <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Portable_Ops" title="Metal Gear Solid: Portable Ops">Metal Gear Solid: Portable Ops</a></i> has him briefly alluded in a <a href="/wiki/Precognition" title="Precognition">prophetic vision</a> as <a href="/wiki/Naked_Snake" class="mw-redirect" title="Naked Snake">Naked Snake</a>'s "son [who] will save the world" (after Liquid and/or Solidus as Big Boss's "son [who] will bring the world to ruin"),<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Peace_Walker" title="Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker">Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker</a></i> shows <a href="/wiki/List_of_characters_in_the_Metal_Gear_series#Master_Miller" class="mw-redirect" title="List of characters in the Metal Gear series">Kazuhira Miller</a> mentioning the "twin sons" that are two years old at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Solid Snake is featured/mentioned in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_Ground_Zeroes" title="Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes">Metal Gear Solid V: Ground Zeroes</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_V:_The_Phantom_Pain" title="Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain">Metal Gear Solid V: The Phantom Pain</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The unlockable bonus mission "Déjà Vu" on the PlayStation platform and later Xbox platform of <i>Ground Zeroes</i> in which Naked Snake must re-enact situations from the original <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> game and answer a series of trivia questions after fulfilling the mission. If all the questions are answered correctly on the Normal difficulty setting, the mission can be replayed with his low-polygon model from <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> in place of his father's standard character model. <i>The Phantom Pain</i> also shows that his low-polygon model from <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> can be an alternate outfit for <a href="/wiki/Venom_Snake" class="mw-redirect" title="Venom Snake">Venom Snake</a> after transferring the save data from <i>Ground Zeroes</i>. David is also alluded to in association with Eli during a conversation between Big Boss and Revolver Ocelot.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other_Metal_Gear_media">Other <i>Metal Gear</i> media</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other Metal Gear media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Solid Snake also serves as the protagonist in <i><a href="/wiki/Snake%27s_Revenge" title="Snake&#39;s Revenge">Snake's Revenge</a></i>, a sequel to the original <i>Metal Gear</i> for the NES released for the western market in 1990 and developed without Kojima's involvement. Set three years after the events of the Outer Heaven incident, <i>Snake's Revenge</i> has Snake leading a team of FOX HOUND operatives as they infiltrate an undisclosed enemy base where the Metal Gear weapon is being mass-produced. Snake is addressed by the <a href="/wiki/Military_rank" title="Military rank">military rank</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant" title="Lieutenant">Lieutenant</a> and starts the game already equipped with a handgun and a <a href="/wiki/Combat_knife" title="Combat knife">combat knife</a>, in contrast to the first game, where Snake had to procure all of his weapons on-site.
</p><p>After the success of the original <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>, KCEJ produced a trilogy of <i>Metal Gear</i> spin-offs for portable platforms set in a parallel universe outside the main Kojima-directed series. All three of these portable games were directed by <a href="/wiki/Shinta_Nojiri" title="Shinta Nojiri">Shinta Nojiri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parallel_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parallel-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first of these is <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear:_Ghost_Babel" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear: Ghost Babel">Metal Gear: Ghost Babel</a></i> (released outside Japan as <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>), in which Solid Snake must infiltrate a rebuilt Outer Heaven (now called Galuade) to defeat a FOXHOUND-like team of rogue agents called Black Chamber and destroy a stolen Metal Gear prototype, Gander. Although the actual in-game artwork of <i>Ghost Babel</i> was done by Ikuya Nakamura, Yoji Shinkawa provided the promotional art like he did with the original <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>. In the second of these titles, <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Acid" title="Metal Gear Acid">Metal Gear Acid</a></i>, Snake must retrieve "Pythagoras" from the Lobito Physics and Research Laboratory, in order to satisfy hijackers who have kidnapped presidential candidate Viggo Hach. This mission is complicated by La Clown, an expert mimic who impersonates Snake's contact Teliko, and subtle brainwashing that nearly convinces him that he is Hans Davis, a ruthless scientist that worked at the Lobito facility. He overcomes both and contacts the real Teliko, then destroys the latest model of Metal Gear, <a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_(weapon)#Metal_Gear_KODOQUE" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal Gear (weapon)">Metal Gear KODOQUE</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Acid_2" title="Metal Gear Acid 2">Metal Gear Acid 2</a></i> features a main character who is not the real version, but a clone created from tissue samples of the man from the original <i>Metal Gear Acid</i>, following the events of the Lobito Island mission; the Solid Snake from the original <i>Acid</i> is implied to be dead in the sequel.
</p><p>The character appears in his Old Snake form as a playable character in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Portable_Ops#Portable_Ops_Plus" title="Metal Gear Solid: Portable Ops">Metal Gear Solid: Portable Ops Plus</a></i>, a stand-alone expansion to the <i>Portable Ops</i> focusing on online play. In <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Rising:_Revengeance" title="Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance">Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance</a></i>, the VR Missions DLC add-on for the game's Japanese version includes a new weapon that can be used by Raiden known as the <i>Hebidamashi</i>, a talking wooden sword which speaks with Solid Snake's voice (as portrayed by Akio Ōtsuka); the weapon was never made available for the English version.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Outside video games, Solid Snake appeared in the <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> audio drama that focuses on his missions following the battle from Shadow Moses.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He also appears in Alex Garner's <a href="/wiki/Graphic_novel" title="Graphic novel">comic book adaptations</a> of <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> and <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2007_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2007-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Benson" title="Raymond Benson">Raymond Benson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Novelization" title="Novelization">novelizations</a> of these two games also feature Solid Snake; Benson's adaptation of the character frequently focuses on the comical aspects of his characterization.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He also appears in <a href="/wiki/Project_Itoh" title="Project Itoh">Project Itoh</a>'s novelization from <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i> where his actions are told from Hal Emmerich's point of view.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Other_video_games_and_media">Other video games and media</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other video games and media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Worlds_of_Power" title="Worlds of Power">Worlds of Power</a> novelization series created by <a href="/wiki/F.X._Nine" class="mw-redirect" title="F.X. Nine">F.X. Nine</a>, Solid Snake appears in the second in the series, based on <i>Metal Gear</i>. In the book, written by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_Frost&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexander Frost (page does not exist)">Alexander Frost</a>, he is Marine Captain Justin Halley.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This version of the character is non-canon and is not referenced by other versions.
</p><p>Solid Snake has appeared in a number of other games, including other Konami games. Hideo Kojima makes a habit of referencing his previous work. In the Kojima-produced <i><a href="/wiki/Boktai_2:_Solar_Boy_Django" title="Boktai 2: Solar Boy Django">Boktai 2: Solar Boy Django</a></i> (and <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Bokura_no_Taiy%C5%8D:_Gyakush%C5%AB_no_Sabata" class="mw-redirect" title="Shin Bokura no Taiyō: Gyakushū no Sabata">Shin Bokura no Taiyō: Gyakushū no Sabata</a></i>), Snake appears as an unnamed character who sells items to the player. Konami's <i><a href="/wiki/Evolution_Skateboarding" title="Evolution Skateboarding">Evolution Skateboarding</a></i> features Snake and Raiden as hidden characters, as well as two stages set in the Big Shell (the skateboarding minigame in <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_2:_Sons_of_Liberty#Substance" title="Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of Liberty">Metal Gear Solid 2: Substance</a></i> is a demo of <i>Evolution Skateboarding</i> composed exclusively of these elements).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Solid Snake also appears in both halves of a crossover between the <i>Metal Gear</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ape_Escape" title="Ape Escape">Ape Escape</a></i> franchises: the <i>Ape Escape</i> monkeys appear with Solid Snake in the "Snake vs. Monkey" minigame featured in <i>Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater</i>. In turn, Snake appears in the corresponding <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> minigame featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Ape_Escape_3" title="Ape Escape 3">Ape Escape 3</a></i>, where he is rescued by Pipo Snake (Snake's character design in this minigame is taken directly from Naked Snake's).
</p><p>He has also appeared in several cross-company fighting games. In <i><a href="/wiki/DreamMix_TV_World_Fighters" title="DreamMix TV World Fighters">DreamMix TV World Fighters</a></i>, Solid Snake appears as a playable character alongside other <a href="/wiki/Konami" title="Konami">Konami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Soft" title="Hudson Soft">Hudson Soft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Takara" title="Takara">Takara</a> characters such as <a href="/wiki/Bomberman" title="Bomberman">Bomberman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Optimus_Prime" title="Optimus Prime">Optimus Prime</a>. Similarly, in <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Brawl" title="Super Smash Bros. Brawl">Super Smash Bros. Brawl</a></i>, the third installment from the popular fighting game series <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros." title="Super Smash Bros.">Super Smash Bros.</a></i>, Solid Snake appeared as a playable fighter alongside <a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a> character <a href="/wiki/Sonic_the_Hedgehog_(character)" title="Sonic the Hedgehog (character)">Sonic the Hedgehog</a> and a variety of characters from <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> franchises such as <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario_(series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Super Mario (series)">Mario</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Zelda" title="The Legend of Zelda">The Legend of Zelda</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Donkey_Kong_(series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Donkey Kong (series)">Donkey Kong</a></i>. <i>Brawl</i> Director <a href="/wiki/Masahiro_Sakurai" title="Masahiro Sakurai">Masahiro Sakurai</a> has stated that Snake was included under Kojima's request, and that he had talked to Sakurai about adding Snake to the roster of the previous game <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Melee" title="Super Smash Bros. Melee">Super Smash Bros. Melee</a></i>, which did not materialize due to the game being too far into production.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake returned as a playable fighter in <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Ultimate" title="Super Smash Bros. Ultimate">Super Smash Bros. Ultimate</a></i>, after being absent in <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._for_Nintendo_3DS_and_Wii_U" title="Super Smash Bros. for Nintendo 3DS and Wii U">Super Smash Bros. for Nintendo 3DS and Wii U</a></i>. In addition, Snake has appeared as a playable character in other Konami crossover titles, such as <i><a href="/wiki/New_International_Track_%26_Field" title="New International Track &amp; Field">New International Track &amp; Field</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Bomberman_R" title="Super Bomberman R">Super Bomberman R</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-trackandfield_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trackandfield-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Old Snake has appeared in the Japanese version of <i><a href="/wiki/Scribblenauts_(video_game)" title="Scribblenauts (video game)">Scribblenauts</a></i>, having been published by Konami in that region.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Customizations in Media Molecule's <i><a href="/wiki/LittleBigPlanet_(PlayStation_3)" class="mw-redirect" title="LittleBigPlanet (PlayStation 3)">LittleBigPlanet</a></i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> allow the player character, Sackboy, to take on the appearance of Old Snake.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In December 2020, <a href="/wiki/Paul_W._Anderson" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul W. Anderson">Paul W. Anderson</a> stated that his 2020 film <i><a href="/wiki/Monster_Hunter_(film)" title="Monster Hunter (film)">Monster Hunter</a></i> had been based on a 2010 <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid:_Peace_Walker" title="Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker">Metal Gear Solid: Peace Walker</a></i> crossover event with <i><a href="/wiki/Monster_Hunter_Freedom_Unite" title="Monster Hunter Freedom Unite">Monster Hunter Freedom Unite</a></i>, in which a military squad briefly faced monsters from the <a href="/wiki/Monster_Hunter" title="Monster Hunter"><i>Monster Hunter</i> series</a>, with Snake's equivalent in the narrative, <a href="/wiki/US_Army_Ranger" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army Ranger">US Army Ranger</a> Artemis, being portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Milla_Jovovich" title="Milla Jovovich">Milla Jovovich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Solid Snake appears as an outfit in <i><a href="/wiki/Fortnite" title="Fortnite">Fortnite</a></i> as the "Bonus Outfit" of <a href="/wiki/Fortnite_seasonal_events#Chapter_5" title="Fortnite seasonal events">Chapter 5 Season 1's</a> <a href="/wiki/Battle_pass" title="Battle pass">battle pass</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and was unlockable by completing <a href="/wiki/Quest_(video_games)" title="Quest (video games)">in-game quests</a> from January 23, 2024 through March 8, 2024, the end of that season.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Creation_and_development">Creation and development</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Creation and development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224211176">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:30em; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>"The name 'Snake' in <i>MGS</i> comes from creeping up on someone silently like a snake. The adjective 'Solid' expresses Snake's strong and blade-sharp image - paradoxical when combined with a snake's litheness. Normally, 'snake' and 'solid' do not go together. It's like talking about 'hot ice.' I came up with the name to express this lack of balance and equilibrium. But when I decided the codename would be Snake, the character was more Plissken than snake-like at the subconscious level. If I had used a different name for 'Snake' in <i>MGS</i>, he probably would have been a totally different character."
</p>
</blockquote>
<div style="padding-bottom: 0; padding-top: 0.5em"><cite class="left-aligned" style="">– Hideo Kojima<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></cite></div>
</div>
<p>Solid Snake was apparently named after the fictional special forces operative <a href="/wiki/Snake_Plissken" title="Snake Plissken">Snake Plissken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Russell" title="Kurt Russell">Kurt Russell</a>'s character in <i><a href="/wiki/Escape_from_New_York" title="Escape from New York">Escape from New York</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kent_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kent-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-interview_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interview-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, Kojima revealed in March 2014 that the character's name origins were something else. According to Kojima, he was given the "Snake" name because snakes are a symbol of stealth. Additionally, the "Solid" part of his code-name was given to give the opposite impression of a soft image.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kojima has compared Snake's personality with <a href="/wiki/Lupin_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Lupin III">Lupin III</a> of <a href="/wiki/Monkey_Punch" title="Monkey Punch">Monkey Punch</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lupin_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Lupin III">Lupin III</a></i> franchise, stating that in "<i>MGS</i>, Snake became this sharp-tongued, Lupin III-like guy who flirted with women and told lots of jokes".<sup id="cite_ref-1up_famitsu_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_famitsu-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His real name David<sup id="cite_ref-mynameisdavid_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mynameisdavid-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a tribute to the film <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> that has a character with the same name (and coincidentally shared with his English voice actor <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Making_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Making-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kojima later described Snake's role in the original <i>Metal Gear</i> as the "player's presence", contrasting the defined personality acquired in <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}@media screen{html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:272px;max-width:272px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:136px;max-width:136px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:172px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Hideo_Kojima_-_Tokyo_Game_Show_2011_(1)_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hideo_Kojima_-_Tokyo_Game_Show_2011_%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Hideo_Kojima_-_Tokyo_Game_Show_2011_%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="134" height="172" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hideo_Kojima_-_Tokyo_Game_Show_2011_%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Hideo_Kojima_-_Tokyo_Game_Show_2011_%281%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="641" data-file-height="823" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:172px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Yoji_Shinkawa.png" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Yoji_Shinkawa.png/250px-Yoji_Shinkawa.png" decoding="async" width="130" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Yoji_Shinkawa.png/330px-Yoji_Shinkawa.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="600" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Solid Snake was created by <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a> (left) and designed by <a href="/wiki/Yoji_Shinkawa" title="Yoji Shinkawa">Yoji Shinkawa</a> (right).</div></div></div></div>
<p>In addition to expanding Solid Snake's backstory, as the first <i>Metal Gear</i> game to feature voice acting, <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> established his characteristic voice and appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-retroactive_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retroactive-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Various scenes from the games relate Solid Snake's ideals with Hideo Kojima's. During <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i>, Snake encourages Raiden to trust himself in making his own choices with the former representing the veteran developer and the latter the younger staff who are to decide whether a sequel to the series would be made without Kojima.<sup id="cite_ref-Making_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Making-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i>, Snake tries to protect the next generation by stopping Ocelot which represented Kojima working with the staff to avoid bugs from occurring within the game.<sup id="cite_ref-solidfourmaking_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solidfourmaking-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kojima introduced the cloning origins of Snake to <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> in order to provide Snake with an adversary who would be his equal, since the story, being a continuation of the original MSX2 games, established Snake as an experienced soldier.<sup id="cite_ref-tgs07_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgs07-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kojima explained that his decision to introduce a new playable character in Snake's place for <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i> was done in order to develop Snake from another character's perspective, but also to avoid treating Snake as a rookie by having a new character be instructed via Codec instead.<sup id="cite_ref-finalhoursofmgs2_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalhoursofmgs2-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake was written to act as father figure not only to protect those he cares but also leave a message for the future generation despite his imminent death. As a pacifist message, Snake's stress increases when killing enemies.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Snake and Otacon were meant to die in the game, with Kojima being inspired by the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Sacco_%26_Vanzetti" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacco &amp; Vanzetti">Sacco &amp; Vanzetti</a></i> in regards to how the duo use death as a penalty for how they are criminals rather than heroes. While the novel retained this idea, the ending in the game was changed with Snake and Otacon surviving.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Following Kojima's departure from Konami, the company indicated that it does not intend to produce further <i>Metal Gear</i> games with Solid Snake as the protagonist;<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Kojima has himself stated that Solid Snake "is one character that I don't want to entrust to other people".<sup id="cite_ref-tgs07_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgs07-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Design">Design</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Design"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Damme_Cannes_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Van_Damme_Cannes_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Van_Damme_Cannes_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="360" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Van_Damme_Cannes_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="529" /></a><figcaption>The Solid Snake design created by <a href="/wiki/Yoji_Shinkawa" title="Yoji Shinkawa">Yoji Shinkawa</a> for <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> is inspired by actors <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Van_Damme" title="Jean-Claude Van Damme">Jean-Claude Van Damme</a> (pictured) and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Walken" title="Christopher Walken">Christopher Walken</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Much as <i>Metal Gear</i> began as a <a href="/wiki/Genre_parodies" class="mw-redirect" title="Genre parodies">pastiche</a> of <a href="/wiki/Action_film" title="Action film">action movies</a> of the time, Solid Snake began as a pastiche of action movie heroes. On the cover artwork of the original <i>Metal Gear</i> he resembles actor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Biehn" title="Michael Biehn">Michael Biehn</a> as <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Reese" title="Kyle Reese">Kyle Reese</a> in the 1984 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terminator" title="The Terminator">The Terminator</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Saga_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although Kojima claimed to have no involvement in the production of the game's packaging illustration.<sup id="cite_ref-kojimaonmg1cover_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kojimaonmg1cover-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the in-game portrait of <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_2:_Solid_Snake" title="Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake">Metal Gear 2: Solid Snake</a></i>, he resembles <a href="/wiki/Mel_Gibson" title="Mel Gibson">Mel Gibson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Saga_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saga-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Yoji_Shinkawa" title="Yoji Shinkawa">Yoji Shinkawa</a>'s Solid Snake design, characterized by his navy blue bandanna and "sneaking suit", would serve as the template for all future incarnations in later <i>Metal Gear</i> games. According to Shinkawa, Snake's physique in <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> was based on that of action star <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Van_Damme" title="Jean-Claude Van Damme">Jean-Claude Van Damme</a>, while his facial appearance inspired by actor <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Walken" title="Christopher Walken">Christopher Walken</a>. Shinkawa described his rendition of Solid Snake from <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> as a "middle ground" between the younger Snake who was in the cover artwork of the first <i>Metal Gear</i> and the middle-aged Snake from the MSX2 version of <i>Metal Gear 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-interview_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interview-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For the initial events from the Big Shell chapter from <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i>, Snake's visual appearance was sightly modified with his hair being more blonde, and his appearance somewhat resembling the <a href="/wiki/Man_with_No_Name" title="Man with No Name">Man with No Name</a> (as portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Clint_Eastwood" title="Clint Eastwood">Clint Eastwood</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Shinkawa commented that Snake was one of the easiest <i>Metal Gear</i> characters for him to draw, as his appearance is consistent across games with only minor changes.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Kojima, Snake's character model was specifically designed to have a well-sculpted buttocks, as the player spends the majority of the game staring at the character's back from a <a href="/wiki/Third-person_view" class="mw-redirect" title="Third-person view">third-person view</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>By the time <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i> started development, Kojima told Shinkawa about his idea of making Snake look elderly, which surprised the designer. Once Shinkawa showed his artwork of Old Snake to the staff, they were all also surprised by the idea of playing as an old version of the character. However, they were satisfied with the end product as the staff began to like the character.<sup id="cite_ref-solidfourmaking_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solidfourmaking-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i>, one of Kojima's endings would have had Snake and Otacon turn themselves in for breaking the law, and subsequently they would be convicted and executed.<sup id="cite_ref-tgs07_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgs07-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, comments from Kojima's staff who were disappointed with his death resulted in the character's survival.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In <i>Metal Gear Solid 4</i>, Old Snake is modelled after <a href="/wiki/Lee_Van_Cleef" title="Lee Van Cleef">Lee Van Cleef</a> who appeared in <i>Escape from New York</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Voice_actors">Voice actors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Voice actors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1273380762/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" /><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:272px;max-width:272px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:136px;max-width:136px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:148px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Akio_Otsuka_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Akio_Otsuka_2018.jpg/250px-Akio_Otsuka_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="134" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Akio_Otsuka_2018.jpg/330px-Akio_Otsuka_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="1165" /></a></span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:148px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg/130px-David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg/195px-David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/David_Hayter_2006-09-21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="233" data-file-height="266" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Solid Snake is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Akio_%C5%8Ctsuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Akio Ōtsuka">Akio Ōtsuka</a> (left) in Japanese and <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a> (right) in English.</div></div></div></div>
<p>In the games, Solid Snake has been voiced by <a href="/wiki/Akio_%C5%8Ctsuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Akio Ōtsuka">Akio Ōtsuka</a> in the Japanese version, and by <a href="/wiki/David_Hayter" title="David Hayter">David Hayter</a> in the English adaptations. When working in <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Planet" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain Planet">Captain Planet</a></i>, Hayter met the casting director of this show, <a href="/wiki/Kris_Zimmerman" title="Kris Zimmerman">Kris Zimmerman</a>, who would later also be the voice-over director for <i>Metal Gear</i> games. When debuting in <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>, Hayter was impressed by the game's cutscenes and the amount of dialogue. One of Snake's lines that Hayter liked was "I just didn't expect a world-class designer of military technology to be so… cute." when Snake interacts with Mei Ling, believing it showed a more fun side of him. Solid Snake's English voice was inspired by Hayter's experience with Japan's storytelling, resulting in minor changes for the script. Hayter himself felt shocked when <i>Sons of Liberty</i> was released as the narrative focused more on newcomer Raiden rather than him. Although there were no news about Snake's future role in <i>Metal Gear</i>, the actor believes <i>Guns of the Patriots</i> gave the character a proper closure.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One of Snake's final scenes in this game bothered Hayter as during the ending the character hesitates to kill himself despite having killed multiple enemies in fights. Nevertheless, Hayter stated that he "loves" the character he was given to portray.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Other than the aforementioned voice actors, Solid Snake has also been dubbed in four different languages for the European localization of <i>Metal Gear Solid</i>; in French by <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Bonami" title="Emmanuel Bonami">Emmanuel Bonami</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in German by <a href="/wiki/Stephan_Grothgar" title="Stephan Grothgar">Stephan Grothgar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in Italian by Alessandro Ricci,<sup id="cite_ref-player_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-player-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in Spanish by <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Vall%C3%A9s" title="Alfonso Vallés">Alfonso Vallés</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Popularity">Popularity</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Popularity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Solid Snake's character was very well received by gaming media. <i><a href="/wiki/Retro_Gamer" title="Retro Gamer">Retro Gamer</a></i> included him in the section "top ten forces of good" in their 2004 list of top 50 retro game heroes.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2005, <i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Gaming_Monthly" title="Electronic Gaming Monthly">Electronic Gaming Monthly</a></i> listed Solid Snake as number one as the top ten video game characters of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Solid Snake appeared in multiple <i><a href="/wiki/GameFAQs" title="GameFAQs">GameFAQs</a></i> "Character Battle" contests, and was runner-up in three: the "Character Battle V" in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  the "Character Battle VII" in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the "Character Battle IX" in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In an <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> poll from 2008, his character was voted as the most popular video game character in Japan, tying with Nintendo's <a href="/wiki/Pikachu" title="Pikachu">Pikachu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i> poll in 2010, Solid Snake was voted by readers as the most popular video game character.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_famitsu_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_famitsu-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His character was amongst the last 16 contestants on the greatest video game hero on <i><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a></i> contest held in 2009, and lost out to <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Freeman" title="Gordon Freeman">Gordon Freeman</a> on a tiebreaker.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records_Gamer%27s_Edition" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness World Records Gamer&#39;s Edition">Guinness World Records Gamer's Edition</a></i> from 2011, Solid Snake was voted as the fourth most popular video game character.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(magazine)" title="Empire (magazine)">Empire</a></i> ranked Solid Snake as the 19th greatest video game character, adding that "beginning as an action pastiche, he swiftly evolved into his very own character".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/ScrewAttack" class="mw-redirect" title="ScrewAttack">ScrewAttack</a></i> ranked him as the <a href="/wiki/ScrewAttack%27s_Top_10" class="mw-redirect" title="ScrewAttack&#39;s Top 10">sixth "coolest" character in video games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/1UP.com" class="mw-redirect" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a></i> listed him second in the list of top video game smokers, while <i><a href="/wiki/GamesRadar" class="mw-redirect" title="GamesRadar">GamesRadar</a></i> placed him at the top of their 2009 list of manliest men in video game history.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> ranked him as fourth on the list of top "pervs" in games in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and as the seventh greatest soldier in video games in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2021, Chris Morgan for <i><a href="/wiki/Yardbarker" title="Yardbarker">Yardbarker</a></i> described Snake as one of "the most memorable characters from old school Nintendo games".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  <i><a href="/wiki/HobbyConsolas" title="HobbyConsolas">HobbyConsolas</a></i> named Snake as third of their "The 30 best heroes of the last 30 years."<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Critical_response">Critical response</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Solid_Snake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Critical response"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Critics have commented on his traits and appearance, often praising Solid Snake for his appealing personality.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Rich Knight and Gus Turner from <i>Complex</i> acknowledged him as one of the best video game mascot, praising his "deep, human emotion that other characters fail to match."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>IGN</i> also remarked their rivalry, saying "Few rivalries in games have spanned as massive and confusing a timeline as Solid Snake and Liquid Snake".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among the several characters he encounters, critics noticed that Snake's friendship with Otacon was one of the best parts of his character due to the contrast it has with enemies as well as how he Snake comforts him in <i>Sons of Liberty</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His rivalry with Big Boss was also popular according to journalists, especially when they are compared as son and father and genetic heir.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Various gaming sites such as <i><a href="/wiki/1UP.com" class="mw-redirect" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Kotaku" title="Kotaku">Kotaku</a></i> joked on the poor relationship between the two of them as the father attempts to murder his own son.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among other character relationships, Snake and Gray Fox were popular due to the variety of enemies the player faces.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Solid Snake's <i>Metal Gear Solid 2</i> design was at the bottom of the worst game character makeovers list by <i><a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a></i>, condemning his conversion in hairstyle in comparison to his <i>Metal Gear Solid</i> design,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and was also at the top of <i><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s list of the worst video game haircuts.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  The book <i>Playing with Videogames</i> states that Raiden's inclusion was intended to surprise <i>Metal Gear</i> fans who, instead of playing as Snake, played as his opposite. Writer James Newman commented that fans' reactions were highly negative; they acted as though Kojima had betrayed their expectations. He compared Raiden to the controversial <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> character <a href="/wiki/Jar_Jar_Binks" title="Jar Jar Binks">Jar Jar Binks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-playingwithvideogames_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-playingwithvideogames-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Eurogamer" title="Eurogamer">Eurogamer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Tom Bramwell commented that his interactions with the other characters also helped expand Solid Snake's character.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> His interactions with veteran Solid Snake identify the former as "a <i>Metal Gear</i> fan". As the game progresses it is stated that Raiden "has become Snake", having developed skills similar to those he gained from taking part in the Big Shell's fights that resemble <i>Metal Gear Solid</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Shadow Moses Island.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear_Solid_3:_Snake_Eater" title="Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater">Metal Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater</a></i>, the character was thought to be the game's protagonist because of his physical resemblances with Naked Snake.
